  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;

  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */

  textarea, select, input {

  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for

          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          flex-grow: 0;

        }

          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);

          overflow-y: auto;

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Dear team,



<span class="line"><!---->Dear team,<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This issue has been reported to Android Security Team with reference (



<span class="line"><!---->This issue has been reported to Android Security Team with reference (<!----></span>





issue #174157709



<span class="line"><!---->issue #174157709<!----></span>





, 



<span class="line"><!---->, <!----></span>





https://issuetracker.google.com/174157709)



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://issuetracker.google.com/174157709)"><!---->https://issuetracker.google.com/174157709)<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>





 The Android Security Team forwarded this issue for you. Here, we submit the issue for you with further details just in case you haven't received it from Android Security Team.



<span class="line"><!----> The Android Security Team forwarded this issue for you. Here, we submit the issue for you with further details just in case you haven't received it from Android Security Team.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





We identified a potential self-XSS issue in Chrome Android mobile browser. The self-XSS vulnerability can be executed from the browser address bar. We're aware that the current practice you follow is to trim "javascript:" when users paste a script from the clipboard.



<span class="line"><!---->We identified a potential self-XSS issue in Chrome Android mobile browser. The self-XSS vulnerability can be executed from the browser address bar. We're aware that the current practice you follow is to trim "javascript:" when users paste a script from the clipboard.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, if a user pastes a script with "javascript:" from the keyboard clipboard, the trimming will not apply and the script will be executed. The keyboard clipboard is supported on all Android devices and available in the keyboard. It can be accessed from the Android keyboard by clicking on the clipboard icon.



<span class="line"><!---->However, if a user pastes a script with "javascript:" from the keyboard clipboard, the trimming will not apply and the script will be executed. The keyboard clipboard is supported on all Android devices and available in the keyboard. It can be accessed from the Android keyboard by clicking on the clipboard icon.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Please check the supplied demo video for further details. 



<span class="line"><!---->Please check the supplied demo video for further details. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Please refer to this older issue and the following URL for further info about self-XSS



<span class="line"><!---->Please refer to this older issue and the following URL for further info about self-XSS<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://bugzilla.mozilla.org/show_bug.cgi?id=1422643



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugzilla.mozilla.org/show_bug.cgi?id=1422643"><!---->https://bugzilla.mozilla.org/show_bug.cgi?id=1422643<!----></a>



<br>





[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-XSS#:~:text=Self-XSS%20operates%20by%20tricking,to%20hack%20another%20user's%20



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-XSS#:~:text=Self-XSS%20operates%20by%20tricking,to%20hack%20another%20user's%20"><!---->https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-XSS#:~:text=Self-XSS%20operates%20by%20tricking,to%20hack%20another%20user's%20<!----></a>



<br>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Chrome Version: [86.0.4240.198] + [stable]



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: [86.0.4240.198] + [stable]<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Android 10, Security patch level Sep 2020.



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Android 10, Security patch level Sep 2020.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Please check the supplied demo video..



<span class="line"><!---->Please check the supplied demo video..<!----></span>



<br>





1.Copy the javascript URL ~ javascript:alert("Self XSS on @ "+document.cookie);



<span class="line"><!---->1.Copy the javascript URL ~ javascript:alert("Self XSS on @ "+document.cookie);<!----></span>



<br>





2.Open Chrome browser and access any web page (email, bank, social messages websites..etc).



<span class="line"><!---->2.Open Chrome browser and access any web page (email, bank, social messages websites..etc).<!----></span>



<br>





3.Click on the keyboard clipboard and choose the copied URL to paste it.



<span class="line"><!---->3.Click on the keyboard clipboard and choose the copied URL to paste it.<!----></span>



<br>





4.Click on the link or Go from the keyboard and the code will be executed.



<span class="line"><!---->4.Click on the link or Go from the keyboard and the code will be executed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





MITIGATION



<span class="line"><!---->MITIGATION<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1.We believe removing the support of "javascript:" might be best to avoid any self-XSS. This is already implemented in Firefox mobile browser, Safari, Desktop Chrome and Desktop MS Edge.



<span class="line"><!---->1.We believe removing the support of "javascript:" might be best to avoid any self-XSS. This is already implemented in Firefox mobile browser, Safari, Desktop Chrome and Desktop MS Edge.<!----></span>



<br>





2.Intercept the keyboard clipboard "paste" action and trim the "javascript:" from the pasted text.



<span class="line"><!---->2.Intercept the keyboard clipboard "paste" action and trim the "javascript:" from the pasted text.<!----></span>



<br>





3.Add a handler to the address bar EditText to clear the "javascript:" string from the inserted text.



<span class="line"><!---->3.Add a handler to the address bar EditText to clear the "javascript:" string from the inserted text.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





CREDIT INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->CREDIT INFORMATION<!----></b>



<br>





University of Birmingham



<span class="line"><!---->University of Birmingham<!----></span>



<br>





Abdulla Aldoseri  {axa1170@student.bham.ac.uk}



<span class="line"><!---->Abdulla Aldoseri  {axa1170@student.bham.ac.uk}<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->David Oswald      {d.f.oswald@bham.ac.uk}<!----></span>

If you are using a webview for Android chromium, maybe you can interecpt the url before loading the page by overiding shouldOverrideUrlLoading method. see the example



<span class="line"><!---->If you are using a webview for Android chromium, maybe you can interecpt the url before loading the page by overiding shouldOverrideUrlLoading method. see the example<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





// Code example



<span class="line"><!---->// Code example<!----></span>



<br>





 mWebView.setWebViewClient(new WebViewClient() {



<span class="line"><!----> mWebView.setWebViewClient(new WebViewClient() {<!----></span>



<br>





            @Override



<span class="line"><!---->            @Override<!----></span>



<br>





            public boolean shouldOverrideUrlLoading(WebView webView, String url) {



<span class="line"><!---->            public boolean shouldOverrideUrlLoading(WebView webView, String url) {<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





                //todo: strip the Javascript: prefix from the url 



<span class="line"><!---->                //todo: strip the Javascript: prefix from the url <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





                webView.loadUrl(url);



<span class="line"><!---->                webView.loadUrl(url);<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





                return true;



<span class="line"><!---->                return true;<!----></span>



<br>





            }



<span class="line"><!---->            }<!----></span>



<br>





        });



<span class="line"><!---->        });<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->1. Fetching the clipboard text and sanitize it before paste it using this method (sanitizeTextForPaste)<!----></span>



<br>





https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/omnibox/UrlBarMediator.java#L279



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/omnibox/UrlBarMediator.java#L279"><!---->https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/omnibox/UrlBarMediator.java#L279<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





2.The method (sanitizeTextForPaste) will call (StripJavascriptSchemas) function from ominbox to strip the javascript scheme at this line



<span class="line"><!---->2.The method (sanitizeTextForPaste) will call (StripJavascriptSchemas) function from ominbox to strip the javascript scheme at this line<!----></span>



<br>





https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/components/omnibox/browser/omnibox_view.cc#L151



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/components/omnibox/browser/omnibox_view.cc#L151"><!---->https://github.com/chromium/chromium/blob/99314be8152e688bafbbf9a615536bdbb289ea87/components/omnibox/browser/omnibox_view.cc#L151<!----></a>

The way Desktop handles the problem is by stripping the leading "javascript:" from the clipboard content when pasting.



<span class="line"><!---->The way Desktop handles the problem is by stripping the leading "javascript:" from the clipboard content when pasting.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If we type in directly "javacsript:alert(document.cookie);" we still get the scrip executed.



<span class="line"><!---->If we type in directly "javacsript:alert(document.cookie);" we still get the scrip executed.<!----></span>



<br>





We won't be addressing that part as part of this issue, given it is not clipboard related.



<span class="line"><!---->We won't be addressing that part as part of this issue, given it is not clipboard related.<!----></span>

I got response back from the Gboard folks (suzhe@):



<span class="line"><!---->I got response back from the Gboard folks (suzhe@):<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





> Unfortunately, I don't think it's something that should be fixed in Gboard. Even if we can fix this bug in Gboard somehow, we can't fix every 3rd-party IMEs which have the similar copy/paste functionality. This bug should definitely be fixed in Chrome.



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; Unfortunately, I don't think it's something that should be fixed in Gboard. Even if we can fix this bug in Gboard somehow, we can't fix every 3rd-party IMEs which have the similar copy/paste functionality. This bug should definitely be fixed in Chrome.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





> I'm wondering why Chrome needs to support executing javascript in the omnibox? Can't we just remove this capability? If we do need to keep this capability for some strong reason, then can we show some alert UI to the user asking for a confirmation before executing the script?



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; I'm wondering why Chrome needs to support executing javascript in the omnibox? Can't we just remove this capability? If we do need to keep this capability for some strong reason, then can we show some alert UI to the user asking for a confirmation before executing the script?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It is also confirmed that GBoard is acting as if the user was typing in the whole message while pasting. Chrome currently allows the input starting from "javascript:" and executes the string directly (On Android and desktop at least).



<span class="line"><!---->It is also confirmed that GBoard is acting as if the user was typing in the whole message while pasting. Chrome currently allows the input starting from "javascript:" and executes the string directly (On Android and desktop at least).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We have 4-ish options:



<span class="line"><!---->We have 4-ish options:<!----></span>



<br>





1. Ignore the problem (the user can see what is in the clipboard before they choose to paste it) -- GBoard has multiple ways of showing the clipboard content before the user "pastes" it.



<span class="line"><!---->1. Ignore the problem (the user can see what is in the clipboard before they choose to paste it) -- GBoard has multiple ways of showing the clipboard content before the user "pastes" it.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Impede the capability to execute scripts typed into Omnibox by hand. (e.g. one extra confirmation dialog) -- Covers other IMEs with similar paste mechanics.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Impede the capability to execute scripts typed into Omnibox by hand. (e.g. one extra confirmation dialog) -- Covers other IMEs with similar paste mechanics.<!----></span>



<br>





3. Remove the capability to execute scripts typed into Omnibox by hand. (never run, e.g. sanitize input to remove javascript: before execution).



<span class="line"><!---->3. Remove the capability to execute scripts typed into Omnibox by hand. (never run, e.g. sanitize input to remove javascript: before execution).<!----></span>



<br>





4. Keep pushing for a fix on GBoard side -- unlikely per suzhe@ (see above) and doesn't cover other keyboard.



<span class="line"><!---->4. Keep pushing for a fix on GBoard side -- unlikely per suzhe@ (see above) and doesn't cover other keyboard.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Adding Adrian to me reason through the options above, please.



<span class="line"><!---->Adding Adrian to me reason through the options above, please.<!----></span>

> It is also confirmed that GBoard is acting as if the user was typing in the whole message while pasting.



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; It is also confirmed that GBoard is acting as if the user was typing in the whole message while pasting.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I did some testing in the debugger and I think we can distinguish between key events and IME-committed text changes. The GBoard paste chip does not go through dispatchKeyEvent() [1], but only through onTextChanged(). And because onTextChanged() is called via super.dispatchkeyEvent(), we could set a flag to determine if the new text was the result of actual keyed entry or text composition.



<span class="line"><!---->I did some testing in the debugger and I think we can distinguish between key events and IME-committed text changes. The GBoard paste chip does not go through dispatchKeyEvent() [1], but only through onTextChanged(). And because onTextChanged() is called via super.dispatchkeyEvent(), we could set a flag to determine if the new text was the result of actual keyed entry or text composition.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/android/omnibox/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/omnibox/AutocompleteEditTextModel.java;l=497;drc=385121b715b153153f7626baf728cbd588250ff7"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/android/omnibox/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/omnibox/AutocompleteEditTextModel.java;l=497;drc=385121b715b153153f7626baf728cbd588250ff7<!----></a>

Re #23: determining if an input is a paste action in the keyboard via timing is not 100% reliable. For example the user may store a piece of javascript in the keyboard's personal dictionary with a shortcut associated to it, and then the javascript snippet can be typed into the app at once by typing the associated shortcut instead. The user can also input a piece of javascript snippet and store it as a clip item in the keyboard, and then the user can input it into the app at once with a single click. If you really want to support javascript execution in the omnibox, then these two cases shouldn't be prevented, because the javascript snippet was typed into the keyboard by the user deliberately.



<span class="line"><!---->Re #23: determining if an input is a paste action in the keyboard via timing is not 100% reliable. For example the user may store a piece of javascript in the keyboard's personal dictionary with a shortcut associated to it, and then the javascript snippet can be typed into the app at once by typing the associated shortcut instead. The user can also input a piece of javascript snippet and store it as a clip item in the keyboard, and then the user can input it into the app at once with a single click. If you really want to support javascript execution in the omnibox, then these two cases shouldn't be prevented, because the javascript snippet was typed into the keyboard by the user deliberately.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Re #24: dispatchKeyEvent() won't be called when typing on an on-screen keyboard, so this approach won't work.



<span class="line"><!---->Re #24: dispatchKeyEvent() won't be called when typing on an on-screen keyboard, so this approach won't work.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





IMO, option 1, 2, 3 listed in #22 are reasonable to me.



<span class="line"><!---->IMO, option 1, 2, 3 listed in #22 are reasonable to me.<!----></span>

Unfortunately, I'm not feeling terribly Wise this morning. :)



<span class="line"><!---->Unfortunately, I'm not feeling terribly Wise this morning. :)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





On desktop platforms, we did pretty explicitly carve out bookmarklets in places like CSP to allow them to continue working and making users happy. I do think that's a use case the product would benefit from continuing to support on desktop. I don't have much insight into usage on Android, but it's also not clear to me that they would run through the same code path. On desktop, they're implemented as a directly browser-initiated navigation, not as typing something into the omnibox. The same seems to be true on Android?



<span class="line"><!---->On desktop platforms, we did pretty explicitly carve out bookmarklets in places like CSP to allow them to continue working and making users happy. I do think that's a use case the product would benefit from continuing to support on desktop. I don't have much insight into usage on Android, but it's also not clear to me that they would run through the same code path. On desktop, they're implemented as a directly browser-initiated navigation, not as typing something into the omnibox. The same seems to be true on Android?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If that's the case, I'd be comfortable preventing folks from typing `javascript:` URLs into the omnibox entirely (on desktop and mobile). We have devtools for folks who choose to poke at pages innards to do so. Unless our friends in devrel agree (cc paulkinlan@ and merewood@), option 3 seems like a fine way way to go.



<span class="line"><!---->If that's the case, I'd be comfortable preventing folks from typing `javascript:` URLs into the omnibox entirely (on desktop and mobile). We have devtools for folks who choose to poke at pages innards to do so. Unless our friends in devrel agree (cc paulkinlan@ and merewood@), option 3 seems like a fine way way to go.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->My understanding of bookmarklet is that we have a bookmark URL set to "javascript:..." at this point.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->I think you can solve the issue similar to what <!----></span>





adetaylor@google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/adetaylor@google.com"><!---->adetaylor@google.com<!----></a>





 proposed (option #5) but without timing. 



<span class="line"><!----> proposed (option #5) but without timing. <!----></span>

You can distinguish between paste event of IMEs and single key event.



<span class="line"><!---->You can distinguish between paste event of IMEs and single key event.<!----></span>



<br>





The commit of IME works differently based on the number of characters of the string (N) according to [1]



<span class="line"><!---->The commit of IME works differently based on the number of characters of the string (N) according to [1]<!----></span>



<br>





(N=1): It sends a key char event like an actual keypress.



<span class="line"><!---->(N=1): It sends a key char event like an actual keypress.<!----></span>



<br>





(N>1): It sends a special key with all the strings (text-pasting case)



<span class="line"><!---->(N&gt;1): It sends a special key with all the strings (text-pasting case)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





You simply need to override the OntextChanged method of omnibox/AutocompleteEditText[2] class as follow:



<span class="line"><!---->You simply need to override the OntextChanged method of omnibox/AutocompleteEditText[2] class as follow:<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





bool flag; 



<span class="line"><!---->bool flag; <!----></span>



<br>





// if flag is true, then it is a multiple character paste. 



<span class="line"><!---->// if flag is true, then it is a multiple character paste. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





public void onTextChanged(CharSequence s, int lengthBefore, int lengthAfter) {



<span class="line"><!---->public void onTextChanged(CharSequence s, int lengthBefore, int lengthAfter) {<!----></span>



<br>





    if(lengthBefore == 0 && (lengthAfter>1) && s.toString().toLowerCase().startsWith("java:"))



<span class="line"><!---->    if(lengthBefore == 0 &amp;&amp; (lengthAfter&gt;1) &amp;&amp; s.toString().toLowerCase().startsWith("java:"))<!----></span>



<br>





        flag = true;



<span class="line"><!---->        flag = true;<!----></span>



<br>





        // It need to be from the start(lengthBefore=0),more than a single character (lengthAfter>1) and begins with Java prefix



<span class="line"><!---->        // It need to be from the start(lengthBefore=0),more than a single character (lengthAfter&gt;1) and begins with Java prefix<!----></span>



<br>





    else



<span class="line"><!---->    else<!----></span>



<br>





        flag = false;



<span class="line"><!---->        flag = false;<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Later on, it is possible to strip the java: prefix in afterTextChanged method like this: 



<span class="line"><!---->Later on, it is possible to strip the java: prefix in afterTextChanged method like this: <!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





public void afterTextChanged(Editable s) {



<span class="line"><!---->public void afterTextChanged(Editable s) {<!----></span>



<br>





    String query = s.toString();



<span class="line"><!---->    String query = s.toString();<!----></span>



<br>





    if(flag) {



<span class="line"><!---->    if(flag) {<!----></span>



<br>





      //strip the java prefix from autoCompleteEditText



<span class="line"><!---->      //strip the java prefix from autoCompleteEditText<!----></span>



<br>





    }



<span class="line"><!---->    }<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

It is about pasting a Javascript in the address bar. 



<span class="line"><!---->It is about pasting a Javascript in the address bar. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The default case is, if a user uses the context menu for pasting the malicious javascript, Omnibox will trim the javascript prefix, preventing it from executing it.



<span class="line"><!---->The default case is, if a user uses the context menu for pasting the malicious javascript, Omnibox will trim the javascript prefix, preventing it from executing it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





While here, in this issue, if the user uses the GBoard clipboard to paste the malicious javascript, Omnibox will not trim the Javascript assuming the user enters the text manually.

[Omnibox] Disallow pasting of javascript in the Omnibox



<span class="line"><!---->[Omnibox] Disallow pasting of javascript in the Omnibox<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Currently, if a user copy-and-paste javascript to Omnibox by ctrl+C or



<span class="line"><!---->Currently, if a user copy-and-paste javascript to Omnibox by ctrl+C or<!----></span>



<br>





long press and then select "Paste", the "javascript:" will be striped



<span class="line"><!---->long press and then select "Paste", the "javascript:" will be striped<!----></span>



<br>





from the text by OmniboxView::SanitizeTextForPaste. This sanitizing text



<span class="line"><!---->from the text by OmniboxView::SanitizeTextForPaste. This sanitizing text<!----></span>



<br>





is for the all platforms.



<span class="line"><!---->is for the all platforms.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But on Android, some IME, like GBoard may paste the text as user's



<span class="line"><!---->But on Android, some IME, like GBoard may paste the text as user's<!----></span>



<br>





typing, not from system clipboard. To handle this case, we need to



<span class="line"><!---->typing, not from system clipboard. To handle this case, we need to<!----></span>



<br>





specially handle the case.



<span class="line"><!---->specially handle the case.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In this CL, AutocompleteEditText will count a user's input as the paste



<span class="line"><!---->In this CL, AutocompleteEditText will count a user's input as the paste<!----></span>



<br>





if AutocompleteEditText receive a lot of text in a single call, and then



<span class="line"><!---->if AutocompleteEditText receive a lot of text in a single call, and then<!----></span>



<br>





sanitize the text.



<span class="line"><!---->sanitize the text.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>

Thank you for this report. While we don't consider this to be a security issue that is in our direct threat model, we do appreciate this report and that it enable us to make a rather large functional change that could impact the user security workflow/experience. The Chrome VRP would like to extend a $500 thank you for this report. A member of our finance team will be in touch to arrange payment. Thank you for your efforts and reporting this issue to us and we appreciate your patience during the time between reporting to the fix.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;

          border-spacing: 0;

          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
